indexes</span></a></li><li class="theme-doc-sidebar-item-link theme-doc-sidebar-item-link-level-2 menu__list-item"><a class="menu__link" tabindex="0" href="/weaviate/tutorials/tokenization"><span title="Configure tokenization for keyword search" class="linkLabel_WmDU">Configure tokenization for keyword search</span></a></li><li class="theme-doc-sidebar-item-link theme-doc-sidebar-item-link-level-2 menu__list-item"><a class="menu__link" tabindex="0" href="/weaviate/tutorials/rbac"><span title="Setting up RBAC in Weaviate" class="linkLabel_WmDU">Setting up RBAC in Weaviate</span></a></li><li class="theme-doc-sidebar-item-link theme-doc-sidebar-item-link-level-2 menu__list-item"><a class="menu__link" tabindex="0" href="/weaviate/tutorials/tls-ssl"><span collection migration with aliases</span></a></li><li class="theme-doc-sidebar-item-link theme-doc-sidebar-item-link-level-2 menu__list-item"><a class="menu__link" tabindex="0" class="theme-doc-sidebar-item-link theme-doc-sidebar-item-link-level-2 menu__list-item"><a class="menu__link" tabindex="0" href="/weaviate/tutorials/spark-connector"><span title="Load data into Weaviate with Spark" class="linkLabel_WmDU">Load data into Weaviate with Spark</span></a></li></ul></li></ul></nav><button type="button" title="Collapse sidebar" aria-label="Collapse sidebar" class="button button--secondary button--outline collapseSidebarButton_PEFL"><svg width="20" height="20" aria-hidden="true" class="collapseSidebarButtonIcon_kv0_"><g fill="#7a7a7a"><path d="M9.992 10.023c0 .2-.062.399-.172.547l-4.996 7.492a.982.982 0 01-.828.454H1c-.55 0-1-.453-1-1 0-.2.059-.403.168-.551l4.629-6.942L.168 3.078A.939.939 0 010 2.528c0-.548.45-.997 1-.997h2.996c.352 0 .649.18.828.45L9.82 9.472c.11.148.172.347.172.55zm0 0"></path><path d="M19.98 10.023c0 .2-.058.399-.168.547l-4.996 7.492a.987.987 0 01-.828.454h-3c-.547 0-.996-.453-.996-1 0"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></aside><main class="docMainContainer_TBSr"><div class="container padding-top--md padding-bottom--lg"><div class="row"><div class="col docItemCol_z5aJ"><div class="docItemContainer_c0TR"><article><nav class="theme-doc-breadcrumbs breadcrumbsContainer_Z_bl" aria-label="Breadcrumbs"><ul class="breadcrumbs"><li class="breadcrumbs__item"><a class="breadcrumbs__link" href="/weaviate/tutorials"><span>Tutorials</span></a></li><li class="breadcrumbs__item breadcrumbs__item--active"><span class="breadcrumbs__link">Multi-vector embeddings (ColBERT, ColPali, etc.)</span></li></ul></nav><div class="tocCollapsible_ETCw theme-doc-toc-mobile tocMobile_ITEo"><button type="button" class="clean-btn tocCollapsibleButton_TO0P">On this page</button></div><div class="theme-doc-markdown markdown"><header><h1>Multi-vector embeddings (ColBERT, ColPali, etc.)</h1></header><p>In this section, we will explore how to use multi-vector embeddings in Weaviate. Multi-vector embeddings (implemented through models like ColBERT, ColPali, or ColQwen) represent each object or query using multiple vectors instead of a single vector. This approach enables more precise searching through &quot;late interaction&quot; - a technique that matches individual parts of texts rather than comparing them as whole units.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="prerequisites">Prerequisites<a href="#prerequisites" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Prerequisites" title="Direct link to Prerequisites" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<p>Before starting this tutorial, ensure you have the following:</p>
<ul>
<li class="">An instance of Weaviate (e.g. on <a href="https://weaviate.io/go/console?utm_source=docs&amp;utm_content=tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Weaviate Cloud</a>, or locally), version <code>v1.29</code> or newer.</li>
<li class="">Your preferred Weaviate client library installed.</li>
<li class="">An API key for Jina AI<!-- -->
<ul>
<li class="">A free, &quot;toy&quot; key can be obtained from <a href="https://jina.ai/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Jina AI</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-tip admonition_xJq3 alert alert--success"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 12 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M6.5 0C3.48 0 1 2.19 1 5c0 .92.55 2.25 1 3 1.34 2.25 1.78 2.78 2 4v1h5v-1c.22-1.22.66-1.75 2-4 .45-.75 1-2.08 1-3 0-2.81-2.48-5-5.5-5zm3.64 7.48c-.25.44-.47.8-.67 1.11-.86 1.41-1.25 2.06-1.45 3.23-.02.05-.02.11-.02.17H5c0-.06 0-.13-.02-.17-.2-1.17-.59-1.83-1.45-3.23-.2-.31-.42-.67-.67-1.11C2.44 6.78 2 5.65 2 5c0-2.2 2.02-4 4.5-4 1.22 0 2.36.42 3.22 1.19C10.55 2.94 11 3.94 11 5c0 .66-.44 1.78-.86 2.48zM4 14h5c-.23 1.14-1.3 2-2.5 2s-2.27-.86-2.5-2z"></path></svg></span>See the Quickstart guide</div><div class="admonitionContent_BuS1"><p>For information on how to set up Weaviate and install the client library, see the <a class="" href="/weaviate/quickstart">cloud</a> or <a class="" href="/weaviate/quickstart/local">local</a> Quickstart guide.</p></div></div>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="introduction">Introduction<a href="#introduction" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Introduction" title="Direct link to Introduction" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<p>If you have used vector databases before, you may be familiar with the concept of a single vector representing an object. For example, the text <code>&quot;A very nice cat&quot;</code> could be represented by a vector such as:</p>
<div class="language-text codeBlockContainer_Ckt0 theme-code-block" style="--prism-color:#393A34;--prism-background-color:#f6f8fa"><div class="codeBlockContent_QJqH"><pre tabindex="0" class="prism-code language-text codeBlock_bY9V thin-scrollbar" style="color:#393A34;background-color:#f6f8fa"><code class="codeBlockLines_e6Vv"><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">[0.0412, 0.1056, 0.5021, ...]</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div>
<p>A multi-vector embedding, on the other hand, represents the same object using a set of nested, or two-dimensional vectors. For example, the text <code>&quot;A very nice cat&quot;</code> could be represented by a ColBERT embedding as:</p>
<div class="language-text codeBlockContainer_Ckt0 theme-code-block" style="--prism-color:#393A34;--prism-background-color:#f6f8fa"><div class="codeBlockContent_QJqH"><pre tabindex="0" class="prism-code language-text codeBlock_bY9V thin-scrollbar" style="color:#393A34;background-color:#f6f8fa"><code class="codeBlockLines_e6Vv"><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">[</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    [0.0543, 0.1941, 0.0451, ...],</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    [0.0123, 0.0567, 0.1234, ...],</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    ...,</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    [0.4299, 0.0491, 0.9811, ...]</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">]</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div>
<p>The core idea behind this representation is that the meaning of different parts of the text can be captured by different vectors. For example, the first vector might represent the token <code>&quot;A&quot;</code>, the second vector might represent the token <code>&quot;very&quot;</code>, and so on.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="Single vs Multi-vector embedding comparison visualization" src="/assets/images/single_multi_vector_comparison_light-f0628ab83c2e3e5685a8e076854b639a.png#gh-light-mode-only" title="Single vs Multi-vector embedding comparison visualization" width="4440" height="2720" class="img_ev3q">
<img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="Single vs Multi-vector embedding comparison visualization" src="/assets/images/single_multi_vector_comparison_dark-6b3aa7a93c7dbe4bda6373f44c2da8d6.png#gh-dark-mode-only" title="Single vs Multi-vector embedding comparison visualization" width="4440" height="2720" class="img_ev3q"></p>
<p>Multi-vector representations allow for more nuanced comparisons between objects, and therefore improved retrieval of similar objects.</p>
<p>Weaviate <code>1.29</code> introduces support for multi-vector embeddings, allowing you to store and search for objects using multi-vector embeddings.</p>
<p>This tutorial will show you how to use multi-vector embeddings in Weaviate, using either a <a href="#option-1-colbert-model-integration" class="">ColBERT model integration</a> (with JinaAI&#x27;s model) or <a href="#option-2-user-provided-embeddings" class="">user-provided embeddings</a>.</p>
<p>Jump to the section that interests you, or follow along with both.</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a href="#option-1-colbert-model-integration" class="">ColBERT model integration</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#option-2-user-provided-embeddings" class="">User-provided embeddings</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>In depth: Understanding &quot;late interaction&quot;</div><div class="admonitionContent_BuS1"><p>Late interaction is an approach for computing similarity between texts that preserves fine-grained meaning by comparing individual parts of the text (like words or phrases). Models like ColBERT use this technique to achieve more precise text matching than traditional single-vector methods.</p><br><p>The following visualization shows how late interaction works in a ColBERT model, in comparison to a single-vector model.</p><p><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="ColBERT late interaction vs single-vector visualization" src="/assets/images/colbert_late_interaction_light-fec24c99583d4f5e09e20f0d1196060b.png#gh-light-mode-only" title="ColBERT late interaction vs single-vector visualization" width="5000" height="2000" class="img_ev3q">
<img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="ColBERT late interaction vs single-vector visualization" src="/assets/images/colbert_late_interaction_dark-ac2642601b737d96e45c9f9fac457ca1.png#gh-dark-mode-only" title="ColBERT late interaction vs single-vector visualization" width="5000" height="2000" class="img_ev3q"></p><small>Figure: Late interaction vs single-vector comparison</small><br><br><details class="details_lb9f alert alert--info details_b_Ee" data-collapsed="true"><summary>More about late interaction</summary><div><div class="collapsibleContent_i85q"><p>In a single-vector approach, two embeddings have the same dimensionality (e.g. 768). So, their similarity is calculated directly, e.g. by calculating their dot product, or cosine distance. In this case, the only interaction occurs when the two vectors are compared.</p><br><p>Another approach is a &quot;early interaction&quot; search, as seen in some &quot;cross-encoder&quot; models. In this approach, the query and the object are used throughout the embedding generation and comparison process. While this can lead to more accurate results, the challenge is that embeddings cannot be pre-calculated, before the query is known. So, this approach is often used for &quot;reranker&quot; models where the dataset is small.</p><br><p>Late interaction is a middle ground between these two approaches, using multi-vector embeddings.</p><br><p>Each multi-vector embedding is composed of multiple vectors, where a vector represents a portion of the object, such as a token. For example, one object&#x27;s embedding may have a shape of (30, 64), meaning it has 30 vectors, each with 64 dimensions. But another object&#x27;s embedding may have a shape of (20, 64), meaning it has 20 vectors, each with 64 dimensions.</p><br><p>Late interaction takes advantage of this structure by finding the best match for each query token among all tokens in the target text (using MaxSim operation). For example, when searching for &#x27;data science&#x27;, each token-level vector is compared with the most relevant part of a document, rather than trying to match the vector for the entire phrase at once. The final similarity score combines these individual best matches. This token-level matching helps capture nuanced relationships and word order, making it especially effective for longer texts.</p><br><p>A late interaction search:</p><ol>
<li class="">Compares each query vector against each object vector</li>
<li class="">Combines these token-level comparisons to produce a final similarity score</li>
</ol><br><p>This approach often leads to better search results, as it can capture more nuanced relationships between objects.</p></div></div></details></div></div>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="when-to-use-multi-vector-embeddings">When to use multi-vector embeddings<a href="#when-to-use-multi-vector-embeddings" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to When to use multi-vector embeddings" title="Direct link to When to use multi-vector embeddings" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Multi-vector embeddings are particularly useful for search tasks where word order and exact phrase matching are important. This is due to multi-vector embeddings preserving token-level information and enabling late interaction. However, multi-vector embeddings will typically require more resources than single-vector embeddings.</p>
<p>Although each vector in a multi-vector embedding is smaller than a single-vector embedding, the total size of the multi-vector embedding typically larger, as each embedding contains many vectors. As an example, single-vector embedding of 1536 dimensions is (1536 * 4 bytes) = 6 kB, while a multi-vector embedding of 64 vectors of 96 dimensions is (64 * 96 * 4 bytes) = 25 kB - over 4 times larger.</p>
<p>Multi-vector embeddings therefore require more memory to store and more compute to search.</p>
<p>The inference time and/or cost for embedding generation may also be higher, as multi-vector embeddings require more compute to generate.</p>
<p>Therefore, multi-vector embeddings are best suited for tasks where the benefits of late interaction are important, and the additional resources required are acceptable.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="option-1-colbert-model-integration">Option 1: ColBERT model integration<a href="#option-1-colbert-model-integration" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Option 1: ColBERT model integration" title="Direct link to Option 1: ColBERT model integration" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<p>In this section, we will use Weaviate&#x27;s model integration with JinaAI&#x27;s ColBERT model to generate multi-vector embeddings for text data.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="11-connect-to-weaviate">1.1. Connect to Weaviate<a href="#11-connect-to-weaviate" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.1. Connect to Weaviate" title="Direct link to 1.1. Connect to Weaviate" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>First, connect to your Weaviate instance using your preferred client library. In this example, we assume you are connecting to a local Weaviate instance. For other types of instances, replace the connection details as needed (<a class="" href="/weaviate/connections">connection examples</a>).</p>

jinaaiKey</span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">,</span><span class="token plain">  </span><span class="token comment" style="color:#999988;font-style:italic">// Replace with your inference API key</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">   </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain"> </span><span class="token punctuation" <h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="12-collection-configuration">1.2. Collection configuration<a href="#12-collection-configuration" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.2. Collection configuration" title="Direct link to 1.2. Collection configuration" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Here, we define a collection called <code>&quot;DemoCollection&quot;</code>. It has a named vector configured with the <code>jina-colbert-v2</code> ColBERT model integration.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="13-import-data">1.3. Import data<a href="#13-import-data" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.3. Import data" title="Direct link to 1.3. Import data" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Now, we can import the data. For this example, we will import a few arbitrary text objects.</p>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-note admonition_xJq3 alert alert--secondary"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M6.3 5.69a.942.942 0 0 1-.28-.7c0-.28.09-.52.28-.7.19-.18.42-.28.7-.28.28 0 .52.09.7.28.18.19.28.42.28.7 0 .28-.09.52-.28.7a1 1 0 0 1-.7.3c-.28 0-.52-.11-.7-.3zM8 7.99c-.02-.25-.11-.48-.31-.69-.2-.19-.42-.3-.69-.31H6c-.27.02-.48.13-.69.31-.2.2-.3.44-.31.69h1v3c.02.27.11.5.31.69.2.2.42.31.69.31h1c.27 0 .48-.11.69-.31.2-.19.3-.42.31-.69H8V7.98v.01zM7 2.3c-3.14 0-5.7 2.54-5.7 5.68 0 3.14 2.56 5.7 5.7 5.7s5.7-2.55 5.7-5.7c0-3.15-2.56-5.69-5.7-5.69v.01zM7 .98c3.86 0 7 3.14 7 7s-3.14 7-7 7-7-3.12-7-7 3.14-7 7-7z"></path></svg></span>Embeddings not required in this scenario</div><div class="admonitionContent_BuS1"><p>Recall that we configured the model integration (for <code>text2colbert-jinaai</code>) above. This enables Weaviate to obtain embeddings as needed.</p></div></div>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="131-confirm-embedding-shape">1.3.1. Confirm embedding shape<a href="#131-confirm-embedding-shape" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.3.1. Confirm embedding shape" title="Direct link to 1.3.1. Confirm embedding shape" translate="no">​</a></h4>

<p>Inspecting the results, each embedding is composed of a list of lists (of floats).</p>
<div class="language-text codeBlockContainer_Ckt0 theme-code-block" style="--prism-color:#393A34;--prism-background-color:#f6f8fa"><div class="codeBlockContent_QJqH"><pre tabindex="0" class="prism-code language-text codeBlock_bY9V thin-scrollbar" style="color:#393A34;background-color:#f6f8fa"><code class="codeBlockLines_e6Vv"><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">Embedding data type: &lt;class &#x27;list&#x27;&gt;</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">Embedding first element type: &lt;class &#x27;list&#x27;&gt;</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">This embedding&#x27;s shape is (22, 128)</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">This embedding&#x27;s shape is (25, 128)</span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">This embedding&#x27;s shape is (22, 128)</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div>
<p>Note this in contrast to a single vector, which would be a list of floats.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="14-perform-queries">1.4. Perform queries<a href="#14-perform-queries" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.4. Perform queries" title="Direct link to 1.4. Perform queries" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Now that we have imported the data, we can perform searches using the multi-vector embeddings. Let&#x27;s see how to perform semantic, vector, and hybrid searches.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="141-near-text-search">1.4.1. Near text search<a href="#141-near-text-search" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.4.1. Near text search" title="Direct link to 1.4.1. Near text search" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>Performing a near text, or semantic, search with a ColBERT embedding model integration is the same as with any other embedding model integration. The difference in embeddings&#x27; dimensionality is not visible to the user.</p>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="142-hybrid-search-simple">1.4.2. Hybrid search (simple)<a href="#142-hybrid-search-simple" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.4.2. Hybrid search (simple)" title="Direct link to 1.4.2. Hybrid search (simple)" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>Similarly to the near text search, a hybrid search with a ColBERT embedding model integration is performed in the same way as with other embedding model integrations.</p>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="143-vector-search">1.4.3. Vector search<a href="#143-vector-search" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.4.3. Vector search" title="Direct link to 1.4.3. Vector search" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>When performing a manual vector search, the user must specify the query embedding. In this example, to search the <code>multi_vector</code> index, the query vector must be a corresponding multi-vector.</p>
<p>Since we use JinaAI&#x27;s <code>jina-colbert-v2</code> model in the integration, we obtain the embedding manually through JinaAI&#x27;s API to make sure the query embedding is compatible with the object embeddings.</p>

style="color:#393A34">(</span><span class="token plain">result</span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">.</span><span class="token plain">properties</span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">)</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain"></span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div><div class="flex flex-wrap gap-2 mt-2"></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="144-hybrid-search-manual-vector">1.4.4. Hybrid search (manual vector)<a href="#144-hybrid-search-manual-vector" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 1.4.4. Hybrid search (manual vector)" title="Direct link to 1.4.4. Hybrid search (manual vector)" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>In all other searches where a vector embedding is to be specifically provided, it must be a multi-vector embedding, as with the manual vector search shown above.</p>

<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="option-2-user-provided-embeddings">Option 2: User-provided embeddings<a href="#option-2-user-provided-embeddings" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Option 2: User-provided embeddings" title="Direct link to Option 2: User-provided embeddings" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<p>In this section, we will use user-provided embeddings to populate Weaviate. This is useful when you want to use a different model than one that Weaviate integrates with.</p>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-tip admonition_xJq3 alert alert--success"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 12 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M6.5 0C3.48 0 1 2.19 1 5c0 .92.55 2.25 1 3 1.34 2.25 1.78 2.78 2 4v1h5v-1c.22-1.22.66-1.75 2-4 .45-.75 1-2.08 1-3 0-2.81-2.48-5-5.5-5zm3.64 7.48c-.25.44-.47.8-.67 1.11-.86 1.41-1.25 2.06-1.45 3.23-.02.05-.02.11-.02.17H5c0-.06 0-.13-.02-.17-.2-1.17-.59-1.83-1.45-3.23-.2-.31-.42-.67-.67-1.11C2.44 6.78 2 5.65 2 5c0-2.2 2.02-4 4.5-4 1.22 0 2.36.42 3.22 1.19C10.55 2.94 11 3.94 11 5c0 .66-.44 1.78-.86 2.48zM4 14h5c-.23 1.14-1.3 2-2.5 2s-2.27-.86-2.5-2z"></path></svg></span>Using a model integration with user-provided embeddings</div><div class="admonitionContent_BuS1"><p>Note that if you are using a model integration, you can still provide user-provided embeddings. If an embedding is provided with an object, it will be used instead of the model integration.</p><br><p>This allows you to use any pre-existing embeddings you may have, while benefiting from the convenience of a model integration for other objects.</p></div></div>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="21-connect-to-weaviate">2.1. Connect to Weaviate<a href="#21-connect-to-weaviate" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.1. Connect to Weaviate" title="Direct link to 2.1. Connect to Weaviate" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>First, connect to your Weaviate instance using your preferred client library. In this example, we assume you are connecting to a local Weaviate instance. For other types of instances, replace the connection details as needed (<a class="" href="/weaviate/connections">connection examples</a>).</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="22-collection-configuration">2.2. Collection configuration<a href="#22-collection-configuration" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.2. Collection configuration" title="Direct link to 2.2. Collection configuration" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Here, we define a collection called <code>&quot;DemoCollection&quot;</code>. Note that we do not use a model integration, as we will provide the embeddings manually.</p>
<p>The collection configuration explicitly enables the <code>multi-vector</code> index option. This is necessary to handle the multi-vector embeddings.</p>
<div class="codeDropdownContainer_uCK5 code"><div class="codeDropdownHeader_PNgx"><div class="leftSection_ieqF"><span class="languageLabel_LeYV"></span><div class="languageSelector_Mp0Y"><select class="languageDropdown_BTMK"><option value="py" selected="">Python</option><option value="ts">JavaScript/TypeScript</option></select><img src="/img/site/logo-py.svg" alt="" class="languageIcon_e8S9"><svg class="dropdownArrow_T7wX" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 20 20"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M5.293 7.293a1 1 0 011.414 0L10 10.586l3.293-3.293a1 1 0 111.414 1.414l-4 4a1 1 0 01-1.414 0l-4-4a1 1 0 010-1.414z" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></div></div><div class="rightSection__3jI"><a href="https://weaviate-python-client.readthedocs.io/en/stable" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="apiDocsLink_EDfG" title="View API documentation"><img src="/img/site/logo-py.svg" alt="py docs" height="12" width="12" style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="vertical-align:middle">  API docs</span></a><div class="versionInfo_e5Um"><span class="versionLabel_YSKW">More info<span class="tooltip_vwsi"><svg width="11" height="11" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="currentColor" class="infoIcon_bJII"><path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"></path></svg><span class="tooltipContent_QizM" data-position="left">Code snippets in the documentation reflect the latest client library and Weaviate Database version. <h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="23-import-data">2.3. Import data<a href="#23-import-data" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.3. Import data" title="Direct link to 2.3. Import data" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Now, we can import the data. For this example, we will import a few arbitrary text objects.</p>
<p>Note that in this example, each object is sent to Weaviate along with the corresponding multi-vector embedding. In the example, we obtain Jina AI&#x27;s ColBERT embeddings, but it could be any multi-vector embeddings.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="24-perform-queries">2.4. Perform queries<a href="#24-perform-queries" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.4. Perform queries" title="Direct link to 2.4. Perform queries" translate="no">​</a></h3>
<p>Now that we have imported the data, we can perform searches using the multi-vector embeddings. Let&#x27;s see how to perform vector, and hybrid searches.</p>
<p>Note that <code>near text</code> search is not possible with user-provided embeddings. In this configuration, Weaviate is unable to convert a text query into a compatible embedding, without knowing the model used to generate the embeddings.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="241-vector-search">2.4.1. Vector search<a href="#241-vector-search" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.4.1. Vector search" title="Direct link to 2.4.1. Vector search" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>You can perform a manual vector search, by specifying the query embedding. In this example, we convert the query into a vector using the same (JinaAI&#x27;s <code>jina-colbert-v2</code>) model used to generate the object embeddings.</p>
<p>This ensures that the query embedding is compatible with the object embeddings.</p>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="242-hybrid-search-manual-vector">2.4.2. Hybrid search (manual vector)<a href="#242-hybrid-search-manual-vector" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to 2.4.2. Hybrid search (manual vector)" title="Direct link to 2.4.2. Hybrid search (manual vector)" translate="no">​</a></h4>
<p>To perform a hybrid search with user-provided embeddings, provide the query vector along with the hybrid query.</p>

<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="summary">Summary<a href="#summary" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Summary" title="Direct link to Summary" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<p>This tutorial showed how to use multi-vector embeddings in Weaviate.</p>
<p>Weaviate allows you to use multi-vector embeddings from <code>v1.29</code>, with either the ColBERT model integration, or by providing your own embeddings.</p>
<p>Note that when using multi-vector embeddings, the vector index may need to be manually configured to handle the multi-vector embeddings. This is because the shape of the embeddings is different from single-vector embeddings. This is automatically done when using a model integration such as ColBERT, but must be done manually when providing embeddings.</p>
<p>Once the data has been ingested, you can perform semantic, hybrid, and vector searches as usual. The main difference is in the shape of the embeddings, which must be taken into account when providing embeddings manually.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="further-resources">Further resources<a href="#further-resources" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Further resources" title="Direct link to Further resources" translate="no">​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class=""><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2004.12832" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">ColBERT paper</a>, <a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2112.01488" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">ColBERT v2 paper</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2407.01449" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">ColPali paper</a></li>
</ul>
